Jamison Brereton

44 (398)
All Gods
Avats─Бra K─Б┼Ыyapa, etc.
15 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 14тАУ15

As noted above, Geldner considers this the hardest hymn in the R╠еgveda (тАЬdas schwierigste Lied des R╠еVтАЭ), and a judgment very like this is shared by other scholars (e.g., Oldenberg, who deems most of it тАЬuncertain or hopelessтАЭ [тАЬmeist fraglich oder hoffnungslosтАЭ]). Although in our opinion there are numerous contenders for тАЬhardest hymnтАЭ in the R╠еgveda (X.106, for example, some of which appears to be written in unbreakable code), this one is certainly near the top of any such list.

The difficulties are found in every aspect of the hymn, beginning with the fact that the divine subject(s) of the various verses of the heart of the hymn are never identified.

Then there are lexical problems: a number of rare words or hapaxes; morphological problems, including unusual inflectional and derivational morphology; syntactic problems such as frequent lack of verbs, unclear referents, unclear syntactic roles, and so onтАФnot to mention a general lack of superficial coherence, both between verses and within verses. For all these reasons, the translation given is provisional in general and in many details.

Nonetheless, it is possible to form a hypothesis about what the hymn is тАЬabout,тАЭ and this hypothesis allows one to interpret many of the ambiguities within this framework. Our translation reflects this hypothesis, and in a number of places bracketed identifications have been inserted to guide readersтАФthough we have tried to keep these to a minimum, to avoid too much clutter in the poetry itself, which despite its frequent lack of clarity possesses, in our opinion, both power and beauty, and to allow readers to produce their own interpretations of the hymn.

To be brief, the hypothesis with which we operate is that each verse is applicable to both Agni and Soma, the two crucial deified ritual substances, and therefore many of the verbal contortions are the result of attempting to produce phraseology that is meaningful for each god simultaneously.

(This hypothesis is adumbrated by Geldner in his introduction to the hymn, where he suggests that some verses can be read with intentional double reference to Agni and Soma, though he clearly does not consider the whole hymn in this light.)

The final two verses (14тАУ15), in a different meter and almost mechanically responsive to each other, mention both Soma and Agni, and may be intended as an implicit answer to the riddle posed by the rest of the hymn. In any case, if our hypothesis is correct, the poem is the forerunner of the much later k─Бvya tours de force in which, for example, the plots of the Mah─Бbh─Бrata and the R─Бm─Бyaс╣Зa are narrated at the same time.

The Soma/Agni simultaneity is especially prominent in the first part of the hymn. Toward the middle of the hymn (starting around vs. 8) another theme emerges, that of the poet learning his craft, seeking true speech. What unites the two themes is the sense that poetic inspiration comes from the ritual itself and from the mysteries of the identification of the two most important ritual substances, so that the poet gains his verbal mastery as the sacrifice progresses. But it is also the case that the sacrifice needs his poetry in order to be properly carried through, and so the poetic skill the poet gains from his contemplation of the mysteries of the sacrifice is put to use immediately in the next verses (9тАУ11), and the result always desired by R╠еgvedic sacrificers, the epiphany of Indra on the sacrificial ground, is achieved in verse 12. Because of his contribution to the success of the sacrifice, the poet is lauded in the last verse (13) before the responsive solution to the riddle as the foundation of the whole sacrifice. Thus, the hymn is both a static meditation on a central sacrificial mystery and a roughly chronological progression through the sacrifice.

One of the enigmatic features of the hymn found throughout the hymn is the regular presence of unidentified feminine plurals (vss. 1, 2, 4, 5, 7, 8, 9, 11), especially intriguing in verse 7. Identifying the likely referent(s) for these feminines as the hymn unfolds shows the developing complexity of the hymnic universe of dis course. In the earlier part of the hymn the feminines most probably refer, in the realm of Agni, to the streams of ghee offered into Agni (and also perhaps to the plants he burns)тАФwhile, in the realm of Soma, to the waters that swell the soma stalks and to the cowsтАЩ milk mixed with the pressed soma.

As the figure of the poet joins the hymn, the feminines can have a third set of referents, the insights that provide him with poetic inspiration and the words/songs that result from them. (All of the underlying nouns in all three referential systems are feminine in gender and con ceptually female.) This complex web of reference is beautifully (or dauntingly) on display in verse 11. In our reading of this verse all three sets of feminines are not bound, that is, not in use, when the soma is being brought to the ritual and the sacrifice has not yet started. But when soma the plant is made into soma the exhilarating drink, all three sets of feminines are hitched up: the poetтАЩs words are recited, the streams of milk approach the pressed soma, and the streams of ghee are poured into the fire. The priests direct the various females to their appropriate goals, and at the end of the ritual they are тАЬunhitched.тАЭ

As an aside, we might mention what appears to be a sly joke, located in almost the middle of the hymn (minus the final riddle-solving verses): in 6a, after five verses of exhausting enigmas with many more to come, the poet says, тАЬJust as he appears, so is he said (to be)тАЭтАФan assertion about the transparent clarity of the subject that the frustrated audience may view with bitter irony. However, it is of course not merely a joke, for the poetтАЩs task is to find the hidden mystical truths of the universe and express them in true words, in br├бhman. No matter how superficially baffling, the br├бhman captures how тАЬit really is,тАЭ and so the poet asserts here.

Although numerous puzzles remain in the hymn, we hope to have shown that it is far from тАЬhopeless.тАЭ It can be read as a consistent unity (though the unity we see may not be the only possible one), and, as so often with complex hymns in the R╠еgveda, it is a meditation not only on the ritual but also on poetic craft.

Jamison Brereton Notes

All Gods On the manifold difficulties of this hymn and a possible framework in which to interpret them (as a hymn simultaneously applicable to Agni and Soma), see published introduction.

рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ - рдИрджреГрд╢рдВ рдореЗрдШрдВ рджреЛрд╣рд╕реЗ ред рдХрдореН? рд╡реГрдЬрдирдВ рдмрд▓рдХрд░рдореН рдЙрджрдХрдВ рдЧрд┐рд░рд╛ рдЧрд░реНрдЬрд┐рддреЗрдиреЛрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIn like manneer as the ancient (sages), those our predecessors, as all sages, and those of the present period (have obtained their wishes by his praise), so do you by praise extract (my desires) from him who is the oldest and best (of the gods), who is seated on the sacred grass, who is cognizant of heaven, coming to our presence, vigorous, swift, victorious, for by such praises you exalt him.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 7.12; by such praises you exalt him: Or, anu y─Бsu vardhase may be applied to Indra, you prosper, Indra, by such praises

Jamison Brereton

HimтАФin the primordial way, in the earlier way, in every way, in this way hereтАФ(him who is) preeminence (itself), who sits on the ritual grass
and finds the sun,
him facing toward (our) community will you milk out with song, the swift one conquering (the cows? the waters?), among whom you grow strong.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Save for the fronted pronoun t├бm, this hymn opens with a remarkable series of universalizing adverbs, identically formed with -(├б-)th─Б suffix and linking the current ritual situation (the final one in the series, im├бth─Б тАШin this way hereтАЩ, a hapax) to that of every time and place: pratn├бth─Б p┼лrv├бth─Б vi┼Ыv├бth─Б. This may give us a foretaste of the poetтАЩs laying bare the underlying identity of the two central ritual substances, fire and soma, and of the service accorded them in the sacrifice.

The poet then, in my opinion, produces a red herring: most of the descriptors found in this vs. could apply to Indra – esp. ─Б┼Ы├║с╣Г j├бyantam; cf. ─Б┼Ы├║с╣Г j├йt─Бram of Indra in VIII.99.7. And most interpreters fall into this trap: as Geldner says in his n. 1, тАЬall commentatorsтАЭ identify t├бm as Indra – incl. Geldner himself, Renou, and Oldenberg (Witzel Got┼Н forego referents). However, both Agni and Soma receive these or similar descriptors elsewhere. Agni and Soma are both located on the ritual grass (Agni: III.14.2, etc.; Soma: I.16.6, etc.); both are called svarv├нd- (more often than Indra; Agni: III.3.5, 10, etc.; Soma: VIII.48.15, etc.), jy├йс╣гс╣нha- (Agni: I.127.2, etc.; Soma: IX.66.16, etc.), and ─Б┼Ы├║- (Agni: IV.7.4, etc.; Soma: IX.56.1, etc.). Soma is qualified as j├бyant- (I.91.21, etc.), and though Agni is not modified by this participle, he is the subject of verbal forms of тИЪji (e.g., VI.4.4). All of these are, of course, fairly generic characterizations; the point here is that nothing requires us to leap to the conclusion that Indra is the referent.

Another way to approach the question of the referent of t├бm is to consider what referent is appropriate as an obj. to dohase тАШyou will milkтАЩ – which first may require us to identify the subj. of this 2nd sg. verb (by most lights: Renou takes it as a sigmatic 1st sg., which seems unnec. and doesnтАЩt fit the semantic profile of -se 1st singulars). With S─Бyaс╣Зa. and Geldner, I take it as the self-address of the poet, who will perform his milking task тАШwith songтАЩ (gir─Б╠Б). The middle of тИЪduh generally takes milk (either real or metaphorical) as its object, and both Agni and Soma can be conceived of as milk products – the churning of the fire sticks and the pressing of the soma plant both involve physical actions not unlike milking and what is produced is a fluid or something (fire) that behaves rather like one. Indra is not entirely excluded, however; he could be configured as a cow, тАЬmilkedтАЭ with a praise hymn for him to produce goods. However, as I just said, the milk itself, rather than the cow, is the typical obj. of medial тИЪduh, and so the substances fire and/or soma are more likely referents.

Let us now turn to p─Бda d. This also contains a 2nd sg. med. present, v├бrdhase, in a relative clause whose rel. prn., fem. loc. pl. y─Б╠Бsu, has no possible referent in the rest of the vs. Before turning to that problem, I will first say that I do not consider the 2nd sg. subj. of v├бrdhase to be the same as that of dohase. Instead I think we have switched to the unidentified god/ritual substance referred to by the acc. sg. in the rest of the vs. Although this introduces an interpretational complication, I would point out that in the next vs. (2cd), the god/substance definitely appears in the 2nd person, and note also 8b, which contain a similarly structured rel. cl. тАж y─Б╠Бsu n─Б╠Бma te#, where the 2nd ps. refers to the god/substance. And, most important, the rel. cl. of 1d shows a closer affinity to Agni and Soma than the generic epithets in the rest of the vs. But first we must identify a possible referent or referents for the fem. y─Б╠Бsu.

The standard ploy, which I think is basically correct, is to supply a fem. pl. obj. to j├бyantam тАШwinningтАЩ – generally тАШcowsтАЩ (Geldner, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н). Oldenberg suggests rather тАШwatersтАЩ, which Geldner argues against (n. 1d). Certainly both тАШcowsтАЩ and тАШwatersтАЩ (both fem. pl.) occur as objects to тИЪji – and I see no reason to choose between the two; in fact the reason for not specifying either one is to allow both to be understood, under the neutralizing rel. prn. y─Б╠Бsu. Both Agni and Soma have connections to both cows and waters: Agni is nourished by the streams of ghee (a milk product) poured into the fire, and in a well-known myth he ran away and entered the waters. Soma is mixed with cowsтАЩ milk, as is endlessly emphasized in the IXth Maс╣Зс╕Нala, and before soma is pressed, it is soaked in water to swell the stalks. A third possible fem. pl. referent connected with Agni is plants, in which he is invisible and inherent until kindled. Let us consider some passages whose phraseology resembles our own. In II.13.1 …

ap├бс╕е … ─Б╠Бvi┼Ыad y─Б╠Бsu v├бrdhate Soma, unnamed, тАЬentered the waters among which he grows strong.тАЭ (Note the nearly identical rel. cl.) For Agni cf. I.95.5 … vardhate …

─Бsu тАЬhe grows strong among/in themтАЭ (here prob. = plants); I.141.5 ─Б╠Бd ├нn m─Бtс╣Ы╠Д╠Бr ─Б╠Бvi┼Ыad y─Б╠Бsu … v├н v─Бvrdhe ╠е тАЬJust after that he entered into his mothers, within whom ….

he grew widelyтАЭ (again prob. plants; note that v─Бvс╣Ыdhe, as transmitted without accent, is not part of the rel. cl. If the transmitted form is correct). The connection of a fem.

loc. pl. and a form of тИЪvс╣Ыdh in these passages is striking, and it is Agni and Soma who participate in this phraseology.

Thus, in my opinion, by the end of the vs. the poet has narrowed down the possible referents and set up the rhetorical situation that will dominate the rest of the hymn: an unidentified masc. sg. referent, who can be simultaneously Agni and Soma, and a set of fem. pl. attendants, likewise unidentified, who are connected to the masculine figure.

Griffith

As in the first old times, as all were wont, as now, he draweth forth the power turned hitherward with song,
The Princedom throned on holy grass, who findeth light, swift, conquering in the’ plants wherein he waxeth strong.

Keith

Him, as aforetime, as of old, as always, as now,
The prince, who hath his seat on the strew and knoweth the heaven,
The favouring, the strong, thou milkest with thy speech,
The swift who is victor in those among whom thou dost wax.

Geldner

Aus ihm, dem Barhissitzer, dem Sonnenfinder, sollst du wie in fr├╝herer Zeit, wo die Vorfahren, wie alle, wie die Gegenw├дrtigen den Vorrang f├╝r uns und hinwiederum einen Opferbund mit dem Loblied herausmelken und ein Rennpferd, das K├╝he gewinnt, an denen du nach und nach reich wirst.

Grassmann

Auf alte Art, auf fr├╝here Art, auf alle Art, auf diese Art melkst du [Indra] aus diesem [Soma], der auf die Streu gestellt ist, und Gl├╝ck verschafft, dir Oberherrschaft und Kraftf├╝lle, aus dem hergewandten durch H├╝lfe des Liedes, aus dem scharfen, der die [S├дfte] gewinnt, an denen du erstarkst.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDo you, (Indra), who are radiant in heaven, spread through the regions, for the good (of mankind), those the beautiful (waters) of the unyielding cloud; doer of good deeds, you are the preserver (of men), not (destined) for their detriment; you are superior to all delusions; you names abides in the world of truth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Lovely to be seen for beauty are those (tips [of flame/soma streams]), which are the sun of the lower (realm). (As the possessor) of (those) tips who shines forth (even) for the one who doesnтАЩt impel (largesse), you are a good herdsman, not for deceiving, o strong-willed one. Far beyond the trickeries of magic your name was (set) in truth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

[in this VD seq] and V.63.1, the only attestations in the family books. The putative first member sacca here is then provided with an alternative Sanskritic analysis, s├бc [i.e., s╚зt] ca – IтАЩm not suggesting an emendation here, but a word play.

The second ca connects the underlying bahuvr─лhi to the noun it modifies, hav├нс╕е, hence an underlying sequence hav├нс╕е тАж *sacc├б-dh─Бtu ca. I further suggest that this word play is actualized in a different word in the first word of the p─Бda, ├бtyam, which rhymes with saty├б- (save for accent).

As just noted, p─Бda b participates in a number of phonetic plays: -g─Бtuс╕е echoes dh─Б╠Бtu in p─Бda; s├б h├│(t─Б) anticipates immediately following saho(bh├бriс╕е), and

-bh├бriс╕е is a scrambling of barh├нr in the next p─Бda. This last is particularly worth noting because -bh├бri- is a Vedic hapax (Whitney, Rts., lists it as RV.C., and its only RV occurrence is here) of somewhat unusual formation (see AiG II.2.295). It is clearly a contextually inspired nonce here and should be given no weight in considering i-stem morphology.

The last lexical problem in the vs. is visr├║h─Б in d, otherwise found only in VI.7.6. Grassmann glosses тАШStromтАЩ and connects it with тИЪsru тАШflowтАЩ, which is phonologically impossible (where would the -h come from?). Geldner tr. тАШArmтАЩ, which is just a contextually inspired rendering, as far as I can see. Renou tr. тАШflammeтАЩ (fld. by Kellens, Noms rac. 82-83), though ad VI.7.6 (EVP XIII.127-28) he floats (only to reject) the possibility that it is a variant of v─лr├║dh- (тАШsprout, shoot, growthтАЩ) on the basis of the similarity between VI.7.6 and II.35.8, which contains a form of v─лr├║dh-. This suggestion fits with S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs gloss oс╣гadhi- тАШplantтАЩ (for this passage; in VI.7.6 S─Бyaс╣Зa. glosses the pl. visruhaс╕е as nadya┼Ы ca gaс╣Еg─Бdy─Бс╕е тАЬrivers, Gaс╣Еg─Б, etc.тАЩ). The word has received the most attention from Scarlatta, first in his Root noun book (464-65) and then in the n. to V.44.3 in Witzel Got┼Н (in which Scarlatta is responsible for Maс╣Зс╕Нala V). In the former Scarlatta pronounces visr├║h- тАЬganz unklar,тАЭ echoed by the somewhat less pessimistic тАЬunklarтАЭ in Witzel Got┼Н, where he tr. тАЬReisig und ZweigenтАЭ and suggests itтАЩs derived from *vi-sr-u- тАШsich weit erstreckendтАЩ, contaminated with -r├║dh-, -r├║h-, with the result reminiscent of v─лr├║dh-. I also believe that the word is in the semantic realm of plant growth and that it should be connected with тИЪru(d)h тАШgrowтАЩ; this is esp. clear in VI.7.6, which contains a verbal form of that root: vay─Б╠Бiva ruruhuс╕е sapt├б visr├║haс╕е.

However, I do not think that тИЪsru or тИЪsс╣Ы needs to be brought in, at least directly.

Instead I attribute the extraneous -s- to a sort of analogical backformation involving the preverbs v├н, n├н, and n├нs, starting from the form v─лr├║dh- cited above. Although the lengthening of the preverb v├н in that form results from the initial laryngeal of the etymon of тИЪrudh (see EWA s.v. RODH), it appears synchronically to result from the sandhi form of a byform *vis before r-, just as there is a n├нs beside n├н (with different meanings in that case of course). In particular note the form n─лroh├б- in a TS mantra repeated 3x (III.5.2.5, IV.4.1.3, V.3.6.3 sam╠Рroh├▓ тАЩsi n─лroh├▓ тАЩsi), which could be derived either from ni+тИЪruh (cf. KeithтАЩs tr. тАШdescenderтАЩ) with the same lengthening as in v─лr├║dh- or from nis+ruh (so Vi┼Ыva Bandhu). I therefore explain our visr├║h- as a learned (and/or playful) but false тАЬrestorationтАЭ of the putative *vis- underlying v─лr├║(d)h-. It is here that тИЪsru may have played a part, by facilitating a false segmentation of vis-r├║h- into vi-sr├║h- (on the basis of the phonological similarity of the roots) and thus blocking the application of morpheme-boundary sandhi between

*-s and r-. I tr. тАШoutgrowthтАЩ. On a separate but related note, I do not think we need to emend the form to gen. pl. *visr├║h─Бс╣Г, an idea that goes back to S─Бyaс╣Зa., tempted Oldenberg inter alia, and is accepted by Scarlatta in Witzel Got┼Н.

Having dealt with the details of this vs. piecemeal, we should now consider whether it too can be applied to both Agni and Soma, and the answer is yes. ├бtya- is regularly used of both in passages too numerous to cite. Though Hotar is an esp.

characteristic role of AgniтАЩs, Soma is also compared to a Hotar sometimes (IX.92.2, 6, etc.). Both are called both vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- and ┼Ы├н┼Ыu-. We have already noted their positioning on the barhis ad 1b. Both are called y├║van-. The тАШoutgrowthтАЩ can be the flames of Agni and the traces of the spreading of the soma juice on the filter, often depicted on IX. However, it does seem that Soma is never qualified as ├бjara- тАШunagingтАЩ – a minor lack. The vs. situates both substances on the ritual ground at the moment of the offering.

Griffith

Shining to him who leaves heaven’s regions undisturbed, which to his sheen who is beneath show fair in light,
Good guardian art thou, not to be deceived, Most Wise! Far from deceits thy name dwelleth in holy Law.

рдЗрдпрдорд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдпреА рд╣реЛрддреГрддреНрд╡рдпреБрд╡рддреНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рд▓рд┐рдЩреНрдЧреИрдГ ред рдЕрдпрдордЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдЕрддреНрдпрдВ рд╕рддрддрдорддрдирд╛рд░реНрд╣рдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ рдЖрдЬреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдВ рд╕рдЪрддреЗ рд╕реЗрд╡рддреЗ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ ред рд╕рддреН ред рд╕рддреНрдлрд▓рд╕рд╛рдзрдирддреНрд╡рд╛рджреНрдзрд╡рд┐рд░рдкрд┐ рд╕рддреН ред рдзрд╛рддреБ рдЪ рдзрд╛рд░рдХрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрд╡ ред рд╣реВрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖ рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд╕рд╛рдзрдирддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рддрдпрд╛ рдЪ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЬреЛрддреНрдкрддреНрддреЗрд░реНрдзрд╛рд░рдХрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рддрдерд╛ рд╣рд┐ –‘рдЕрдЧреНрдиреМ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╣реБрддрд┐рдГ рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпрдореБрдкрддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддреЗ ред рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдЬреНрдЬрд╛рдпрддреЗ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд░реНрд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреЗрд░рдиреНрдирдВ рддрддрдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ’ (рдордиреБ. рей. ренрем) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЕрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдЧрд╛рддреБрдГ рдЕрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд┐рддрдЧрдордирдГ ред рд╕рддрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдп рдЧрдордиреЗ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдирд┐рд╖реНрдкрддреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рдлрд▓рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзреЗрд░рд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдЧрдордирддреНрд╡рдореН ред рддрджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╣ред рд╕рдГ рд╕ рдЦрд▓реБ рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реЛрдордирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рджрдХрдГ рд╕рд╣реЛрднрд░рд┐рдГ рдмрд▓рд╕реНрдп рднрд░реНрддрд╛ рдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рдГ рдЕрдиреБ ‘рдкреНрд░рд╕рд░реНрд╕реНрд░рд╛рдгрдГ рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗрдг рд╕рд░рдиреН рд╡реГрд╖рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдХрдГ рдлрд▓рд╕реНрдп рд╢рд┐рд╢реБрдГ рд╕ рдЗрд╡ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгреАрдпреЛрд╜рдкреНрд░реМрдвреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдпреБрд╡рд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рдорд┐рд╢реНрд░рдпрд┐рддрд╛ рдЕрдЬрд░рдГ рдЬрд░рд╛рд░рд╣рд┐рддрдГ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд░реБрд╣рд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд░реБрд╣рд╛рдгрд╛рдореН рдУрд╖рдзреАрдирд╛рдВ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рд╣рд┐рддрдГ рдирд┐рд╣рд┐рддрдГ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрд┐рддрдГ рдПрд╡рдВрднреВрддрдГ рд╕рдЪрддреЗрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe, (Agni), is associated with the perpetual oblation that is the true (source of good); the sustainer of all, he is of unrestricted movement, the offerer (of burnt-offerings), the cherisher of strength; gliding especially over the sacred grass, the showerer (of benefits); an infant, a youth, exempt from decay, whose plural ce is among plural nts.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The steed does the oblation follow (and) its [=oblationтАЩs] elements are true; the Hotar who goes without harm brings might.
Always stretching out along the ritual grass, the bullish child, the
unaging youth is placed in the middle with his outgrowth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Some of the challenges of this vs can be approached by noting the series of phonetic plays it contains: sacate s├бc ca dh─Б╠Бtu ca / dh─Б╠Бtu ca, ├бriс╣гс╣нag─Бtuс╕е / s├б h├│t─Б sahobh├бriс╕е / sahobh├бriс╕е тАж barh├нr.+++(5)+++

Let us begin with the first. The curious double ca phrase s├бc ca dh─Б╠Бtu ca is difficult to render on its own. On the surface it appears to form part of a conjoined NP with the subj. hav├нс╕е тАШoblationтАЩ, but its ill-assorted nature comes out in tr. like GeldnerтАЩs тАЬdie Opferspende und das Seiende und das Element (?).тАЭ Moreover, though dh─Б╠Бtu- does not otherwise occur uncompounded in the RV, after the RV it is masc., while this form must be neut, which would be anomalous if it is a noun here. Geldner suggests (n. 3a) emending to the bahuvr─лhi sapt├бdh─Бtu тАШhaving 7 partsтАЩ (RV 3x), though this is not reflected in his tr. As a bv the neut. gender would be proper, as a modifier of hav├нs-. Renou suggests rather that s├бc ca dh─Б╠Бtu тАЬresolvesтАЭ an old cmpd.

*sad-dh─Б╠Бtu, tr. тАЬet (sa) foundation est r├йelle.тАЭ I am in accord with his rendering but analyze the underlying form differently: I take s├бc ca as a play on MIA sacca-, the Middle Indic product of saty├б-. (That Middle Indic phonological developments are already to be found even in the RV family books needs no further demonstration.) The whole sequence gestures towards a bahuvr─лhi *sacca-dh─Бtu-, whose neut. gender would be appropriate. Note that very similar saty├б-dharman- (RV 5x) is found at

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдпреЛрд╜рд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдЧрд╛рддреБрдГ рд╕рд╣реЛрднрд░рд┐рд░реНрд╣реЛрддрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд░реНрд╕реНрд░рд╛рдгреЛ рд╡реГрд╖рд╛ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдЬрд░реЛ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд░реБрд╣рд╛ рд╣рд┐рддреЛ рдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рд░рдиреБ рд╕рдЪреНрдЪ рдзрд╛рддреБ рдЪрд╛рддреНрдпрдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ рд╕рдЪрддреЗ рд╕ рд╢рд┐рд╢реБрд░реНрдорд╛рддрд░рдорд┐рд╡ рдЬрдЧрддреЛ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рдкреБрдгреНрдпреЗрди рдпреБрдЬреНрдпрддреЗ реерейрее

рдПрд╖рд╛ рд╕реМрд░реА рд╡рд╛ ред рдПрддреЗ рд░рд╢реНрдордпрдГ рд╕реБрдпреБрдЬрдГ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рд╕рдВрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ рдпрд╛рдордиреН рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдЧрдордиреЗ рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрдпреЗ рдПрд╖рдгрд╛рдп рдиреАрдЪреАрдГ ред рдиреАрдЪрдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред ‘рдЕрдореБрд╖реНрдореИ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдп рдпрдореНрдпрдГ рдпрдореНрдпрд╛ рдЧрдордирд╛рд░реНрд╣рд╛рдГ ред рдЕрдерд╡рд╛ рдпрдореЛ рдирд┐рдпрдорд┐рддрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпрдГ ред рддрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдирдГ ред рдЛрддрд╛рд╡реГрдзрдГ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░рд╢реНрдЪ ред рдЕрдпрдорд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпрдГ рд╕реБрдпрдиреНрддреБрднрд┐рдГ рд╕реБрдЧрдордиреИрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╢рд╛рд╕реИрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд╢рд╛рд╕рдХреИрдГ рдЕрднреАрд╢реБрднрд┐рдГ рд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдХреНрд░рд┐рд╡рд┐рдГ рдХрд░реНрддрд╛ рдирд╛рдорд╛рдирд┐ рдирд╛рдордХрд╛рдиреНрдпреБрджрдХрд╛рдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╡рдгреЗ рдирд┐рдореНрдиреЗ рднреВрдкреНрд░рджреЗрд╢реЗ рдореБрд╖рд╛рдпрддрд┐ рдореБрд╖реНрдгрд╛рддрд┐ рдЖрджрддреНрддреЗ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрдерд╡рд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рдирд╛рд╡рд╛рд╣реНрдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрд░реЗрддреЗрд╜рд╢реНрд╡рд╛ рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрдпреЗ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдЧрдордирд╛рдп рдпрд╛рдордирд┐ рд░рдереЗ рд╕реБрдпреБрдЬрдГ рдкреНрд░рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдВ рд╕рдорд╛рдирдореН ред рдХреНрд░рд┐рд╡рд┐рдГ рдХреНрд░рд┐рд╡рд┐рд╕рджреГрд╢реЛрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╡рдгреЗ рдирд╛рдорд╛рдирд┐ рд╣рд╡реАрдВрд╖реНрдпреБрдХреНрддрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрдЬреНрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрдореБрд╖рд╛рдпрддрд┐ рдЖрджрддреНрддреЗ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese well-combined rays (of the sun) are descending with intent to proceed on the path (of the sacrifice), amplifiers of the ceremony for this (its instrumental tutor); operating with these swift-moving, all-regulating rays, he, (─Аditya) steals the waters (that flow) in low plural ces.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These (hymns?) of yours, easy to yoke, (go) forth on their course to seek the twinned sisters [= butter offerings/waters], strong through truth, that (go) downward toward yonder one [=Agni/Soma],
with reins easy to control, directing everything. Krivi [=Agni/Soma/the poet (тЖРkavi)?] steals (their) names [=butter offerings/waters?] at their precipitous fall.

Jamison Brereton Notes

My interpr. of both the syntax and the referents of this vs. generally differs from those of others. I will not undertake a detailed disc. of these differences.

However, I will note that Geldner (n. 4) suggests that both Agni and Soma may be the topic of the vs., in agreement with my general thesis.

In my opinion, a new element enters the ritual scene here, namely ritual speech, referred to by the unidentified et├й of p─Бda a. Given the masc. pl. pronoun, the exact referent must be masc. – perhaps st├│m─Бс╕е тАШpraisesтАЩ (cf. nearby V.42.15 eс╣г├б st├│maс╕е тАж, 16 pra├нс╣г├б st├│maс╕е in the same All God cycle, reminscent of our pr├б va et├й тАж). These praises are conceived of as horses, which are easy to yoke (a: suy├║jaс╕е) and directed by easily controlled reins (c: suy├бntubhiс╕е тАж abh─л╠Б┼Ыubhiс╕е). As Geldner points out (n. 4c with reff.), the reins of priests are their speeches, an association that makes the identification of тАШpraisesтАЩ as the subject of p─Бda a all the more likely. The 2nd ps.

enclitic vaс╕е refers in my view to the priests who are launching/driving the praisehorses. The pr├б тАж y─Б╠Рman тАЬforth on the course/journeyтАЭ invites a verb of motion to be supplied, perhaps a form of тИЪsс╣Ы, suggested by pras├бrsr─Бс╣Зaс╕е beginning the 2nd hemistich of the previous vs. (3c).

The other question confronting us in p─Бda a is the identity of the datival inf.

iс╣гс╣н├бye, which is of course multiply ambiguous: it could belong to тИЪiс╣г тАШseek, desireтАЩ, тИЪiс╣г тАШsendтАЩ, or тИЪyaj тАШsacrificeтАЩ (on this issue, see Oldenberg, ZDMG 62: 473-78 = KlSch 282-87). With Oldenberg, I take it to the first, but I also think it takes an acc. goal/obj., and that that acc. is the fem. acc. phrase in b, n─л╠Бc─лс╕е тАж yamy├а с╣Ыt─Бvс╣Ы╠Бdhaс╕е. Oldenberg also takes this phrase as acc., though he supplies a different verb to govern it; the other interpr.

take the phrase as nom. and the subject of an independent nominal clause. With Geldner (n.

4b) I take the downward-facing twinned sisters to be both the streams of ghee offered into the ritual fire and the streams of water with which soma is rinsed (the milk streams with which soma is mixed could also be in play). The praisesтАЩ seeking of these streams expresses the union of verbal and physical activity in the sacrifice, with the hymns accompanying the pouring of the liquid into/onto the ritual substance. The dat. prn. am├║с╣гmai I take as the goal of this pouring: the fire and the soma respectively. The use of the comparatively rare distal deictic asa├║ is noteworthy, since this stem generally refers to the upward or heavenly world or items located there, esp. the sun (for the sun, cf., e.g., I.105.3, 191.9, VIII.12.30). Yet here the streams are going тАШdownwardтАЩ towards it. This paradox can be resolved by recalling the phrase in 2a ├║parasya тАж sv├ас╕е тАЬthe sun of the lower realm,тАЭ which made reference to well-known conceptions of Agni and of Soma. Agni is frequently considered the earthly counterpart of the heavenly sun, since both blaze brightly and they also make their appearance at the same time (dawn) of the ritual day. Soma, likewise, is often compared to or identified with the sun because of its bright gleam, and there are both a heavenly Soma and his earthly counterpart depicted in the IXth Maс╣Зс╕Нala. Here, in my opinion, am├║с╣гmai makes implicit reference to the heavenly Sun [=Fire] and heavenly Soma, while depicting the ritual activity centered on their earthly embodiments, thus erasing the distance between heaven and earth and the distinction between the entities found therein.

P─Бda d, which I take as a separate clause, brings its own set of problems, not least with the always enigmatic word kr├нvi- (on which see also comm. ad I.30.1).

First, however, note the phonological echo of b am├║с╣гmai / d muс╣г─Бyati, though this does not help with the interpr. As for kr├нvi-, I take it here as a conflation of two putative stems. On the one hand, at least once (I.30.1) kr├нvi- seems to refer to a race horse (there compared with Indra). Since the intertwined Agni/Soma figure in this hymn was just referred to as a steed (├бtya-) in 3a, kr├нvi- here seems to be picking up that joint referent. Geldner [n. 4d] makes the same identification of ├бtya- with kr├нvi-, and he also suggests that the p─Бda expresses the entry of the butter offerings into the fire and/or the streams of water in the soma. I think he is correct as far as he goes, but I think there is a third referent, the poet who is responsible for the praises I suggest are the subject of p─Бda a. In this case kr├нvi- can be seen as a hyper-Sanskritization of kav├н- (as if from *kс╣Ыvi-) with the ri that interchanges with с╣Ы in words like kс╣Ы╠Бmi-/kr├нmi- тАШwormтАЩ (cf. AiG I.33 and Nachtr. 19, 21), aided of course by the kr├нvi- already referring to Agni/Soma. See also disc. ad 9c below.

What does it mean that this kr├нvi- тАЬsteals (their) namesтАЭ? Here OldenbergтАЩs suggestion is surely correct for the Agni/Soma kr├нvi- (for Oldenberg, only Soma): that the streams (of ghee/water) lose their identities when they merge into Agni/Soma, and the result is simply called fire/soma. As for the poet whom I consider the third referent of kr├нvi-, he may тАЬsteal their namesтАЭ by using them in his poetry, or perhaps by referring to them but not naming them, as he does in this vs. (and throughout the hymn).

Griffith

These come, well-yoked, to you for furtherance in the rite: down come the twinborn strengtheners of Law for him,
With reins easily guided and commanding all. In the deep fall the hide stealeth away their names.

рд╣реЗ рдЛрдЬреБрдЧрд╛рде рд╢реЛрднрдирд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдХ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рддрд░реБрднрд┐рдГ рддрд░реБрд╡рд┐рдХрд╛рд░реИрд░реНрдЧреНрд░рд╣реИ: рд╕реБрддреЗрдЧреГрднрдореН рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реБрддреЗрди рд░рд╕реЗрди рдЧреГрд╣реАрддрдВ рд╡рдпрд╛рдХрд┐рдирдореН ред рдХреБрддреНрд╕рд┐рддрд╛ рд╡рдпрд╛рдГ: рд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛ рд╡рдпрд╛рдХрд╛ рд▓рддрд╛рдГ ред рддрджреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рд╕реЛрдордВ рдЪрд┐рддреНрддрдЧрд░реНрднрд╛рд╕реБ рдЪрд┐рддреНрддрдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╣рд┐рдгреАрд╖реБ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд╖реБ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдВрдЬрд░реНрднреБрд░рд╛рдгрдГ рдЧреГрднреНрдгрдиреН рдЧреГрд╣реНрдгрдиреН рд╕реБрд╕реНрд╡рд░реБрдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирдЧрдордирдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдХреЛ рд╡рд╛ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдзрд╛рд░рд╡рд╛рдХреЗрд╖реБ ред рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛рдХрд╛рдиреН рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рд╛рдгреАрддрд┐ рдзрд╛рд░рд╡рд╛рдХрд╛ рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЧреНрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГред рддреЗрд╖реБ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рд╢реЛрднрд╕реЗ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдЕрдзреНрд╡рд░реЗ рдЬреАрд╡рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдЬреАрд╡рдпрд┐рддрд╛ рдкрддреНрдиреАрдГ рдкрд╛рд▓рдпрд┐рддреНрд░реАрд░реЛрд╖рдзреАрд░реНрдЬреНрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрднрд┐ рдЕрднрд┐рдореБрдЦрдВ рд╡рд░реНрдзрд╕реНрд╡ рдЕрднрд┐рд╡рд░реНрдзрдп рее реереирейрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬObject of honest eulogies (Agni), you shine among the reciters of your praises when the Soma is received at its effusion by the wooden (cups), and you accepting (the beverage), are animated by the heart-affecting (praises); giver of life, increase in the sacrifice your protecting flames.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The verse is an extraordinary plural y on words; literally, it reads: seizing with the trees the seized in the effused, the produce of the branching, in the embryos of the mind well-moving, (or) well praised, among the speech holders, straight-sung, you shine, augment the protectresses, the life in the sacrifice

Jamison Brereton

Quivering with your powers of endurance (toward) the one covered with little тАЬtwigsтАЭ that grasps (you) at the pressing [=firewood/sheepтАЩs fleece?], resounding among the clearly pregnant (females [=plants/
waters/cows]),
you beautify yourself at the recitations for the streams, o you with a straight song. Wax strong over the wives, (you who are) alive in the
ceremony.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As usual in this hymn, this vs. swarms with difficulties (Renou calls it тАЬune suite de crucesтАЭ), but it continues to depict a relation between a singular masc. entity and a group of feminines. I see this as the thread that leads us through the labyrinth of this hymn. Note also that, as in vs. 3, there are phonetic figures: ab: saс╣Гj├бrbhur─Бс╣Зas t├бrubhiс╕е … susv├бruс╕е / sutegс╣Ы╠Бbham … citt├бgarbh─Бsu (with mirror-image su). The instr. t├бrubhiс╕е in p─Бda a is a hapax, obviously built to a stem t├бru-. Both Geldner and Renou both take it as тАШtreeтАЩ, which is tempting given the following vay─Бk├нn- тАШtwiggyтАЩ. But II.39.3 j├бrbhur─Бс╣З─Б t├бrobhiс╕е, with the instr. pl. to the better-attested sstem built to тИЪtс╣Э тАШendure, etc.тАЩ, suggests that t├бru- is more likely connected to that root (see on this point EWA I.630). However, I confess that my tr. тАЬquivering with your powers of enduranceтАЭ conveys little sense. I think the instr. here may do little more than reinforce the intensive (that is, frequentative) value of the participle: the subject keeps quivering with continued force (тАЬstaying powerтАЭ).

As usual, I think the subj. of the participle saс╣Гj├бrbhur─Бс╣Зaс╕е is simultaneously Agni and Soma. Agni is elsewhere subject of this intensive (e.g., II.10.5), clearly with reference to his flickering flames. The semantic connection with Soma is not as strong, and Soma is nowhere the subject of this verb, but the scintillating, undulating waves of soma are a common trope in Maс╣Зс╕Нala IX.

Both these substances are aiming towards the vay─Бk├нn-. The most sensible interpr. of that word is as an -├нn-possessive built to an unattested diminutive *vay─Бk├б- тАШlittle branch, twigтАЩ to vay─Б╠Б- тАШbranchтАЩ, hence тАШtwiggyтАЩ (see ScarlattaтАЩs n. in Witzel Got┼Н, referring to his treatment in Rt Noun Cmpds). For Agni this twiggy substance can be brushwood or kindling; the association with Soma is again less straightforward, but it can either refer to the twigs of the soma plant itself or, more likely in my opinion, refer metaphorically to the tufts of wool on the sheepтАЩs fleece filter that catch the impurities in the pressed soma juice. This suggestion is supported by the cmpd modifying it, sute-g┼Хbh- тАШgrasping at the pressingтАЩ. If the vay─Бk├нn- is the fleece filter, it most definitely тАШgraspsтАЩ the solids that accidentally end up in the pressed juice. For Agni, тАШgrasping at the pressingтАЩ is less clear, but the firewood may seem to hold onto the fire burning in it, and the ritual fire burns during the soma pressing.

The rest of the first hemistich consists of citt├бgarbh─Бsu susv├бruс╕е. The standard interpr. all analyze the latter word as containing sv├бru- тАШ(sacrificial) postтАЩ (though note that Grassmann does not provide a gloss for it). Although this analysis works formally, it does not fit easily into the vs. semantically. I am inclined instead to take it as containing a form of тИЪsvar тАШsoundтАЩ; cf. svar├б- (2x, unfortunately with different accent), svar├н-, etc. Geldner (n. 5b) in fact suggests an alternate tr. тАШsch├╢n t├╢nendтАЩ (vaguely following S─Бyaс╣Зa.). -sv├бru- would show the same conversion to a u-stem as the hapax t├бru- in p─Бda a and perhaps follows that word in accent as well. The noisemaking capacities of both Agnia and Soma are well known.

On citt├бgarbha- тАШvisibly pregnantтАЩ see GeldnerтАЩs n. 5b and the TB passage cited there. These females would be, in the Agni realm, the pieces of firewood, which are frequently depicted as having an embryonic Agni inside; for Soma most likely the waters in which the soma plant is soaked, swelling him as their embryo, or perhaps the cows whose milk is mixed with him.

I follow Oldenberg (ZDMG 62 [=KlSch 284 n.1]) in taking dh─Бrav─Бk├йс╣гu as referring to a particular ritual moment, the litanies or recitations when the streams of the oblation are offered, but the equational metaphorical interpr. тАЬrecitations (like) streamsтАЭ found in most tr. is also possible. The voc. с╣Ыju-g─Бtha тАШwhose song is straightтАЩ is somewhat puzzling. I think it is best illuminated by II.26.1 rj╠е├║r ├нc ch├бс╣Гsaс╕е, a phrase I take as a decomposed bahuvr─лhi (see comm. ad loc.) meaning тАШwhose laud is straight on targetтАЩ. I would now slightly alter the tr. here to тАШwhose song is straight on targetтАЩ to make the voc. a little less opaque.

The last p─Бda is surprisingly straightforward, at least for this hymn. The subject of v├бrdhasva is once again Agni/Soma, who derive their strength from their wives (p├бtn─л), the plants/firewood and waters/cowsтАЩ milk respectively.

Griffith

Thou, moving beauteously in visibly pregnant ones, snatching with trees the branching plant that grasps the juice,
Shinest, true Singer! mid the upholders of the voice. Increase thy Consorts thou, lively at sacrifice.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSuch as (the deity) is beheld, such is he said (to be); they abide with concentrated splendour in the waters; (may they bestow) upon us honourable and ample (riches) great energy, numerous male offspring and undecaying vigour.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just as he appears, so is he said (to be): They united (him) with his effective shadow in the watersтАФ
(him) who wins wideness for usтАФ(wins) the great (earth), the broad expanse, and lofty immovable might that brings good heroes.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As I pointed out in the published introduction, the first p─Бda is both a cruel joke – insisting on the utter transparency of the subject of the hymn – and a claim on the poetтАЩs part that his verbal formulations about the subject are in complete conformity with the underlying reality, however obscure they may at first seem.

My interpr. of the rest of this vs. differs significantly in both syntax and semantics from the standard ones, which I will not treat in detail. I take p─Бda b as having an unexpressed masc. sg. obj., with cd further characterizing that obj. The object is simultaneously Agni and Soma, and it is in this p─Бda that the identification of the two is most clearly expressed in the hymn (until the last 2 vss.). The unidentified subj. тАШtheyтАЩ – most likely the poets and/or priests – put together / unite the one (of Agni and Soma) with the other, his counterpart or тАШshadowтАЩ (ch─Бy─Б╠Б-). As the two central deified ritual elements, they are mirror images of each other. The union takes place in the waters (aps├║) for several reasons. Both Soma and Agni have significant presence in the waters – Soma of course through the ritual use of waters both to swell the dessicated soma plant and to rinse it, Agni in two mythological guises, both as Ap─Бс╣Г Nap─Бt and as the runaway ritual fire that hid in the waters.

Moreover, it is also the case that water reflects and was indeed probably the only reflective material readily at hand in this period, so the uniting of one substance and its conceptual equivalent as visual reflections of each other would most naturally take place in water.

The clearest part of p─Бda c is the cmpd. uru-с╣г─Б╠Бm тАШwinning widenessтАЩ, which I take as a modifier of the unexpressed masc. sg. obj. of b (that is, Agni/Soma). (Since the 2nd member is the rt. noun s─Б╠Б-, the cmpd can be masc.) I take the other accusatives in cd, mah─л╠Бm, ur├║ jr├бyaс╕е, and s├бhaс╕е with its modifiers, as objects of an underlying form of тИЪsani /s─Б, extracted from uru-с╣г─Б╠Б-. For a similar play between a root noun cmpd with 1st member obj. and an independent acc. obj., see VIII.1.2 and comm. thereon. Although this syntactic interpr. may seem over-tricky (to others, not to me), it saves us from positing an extraneous creation myth as Geldner and Renou do. In my interpr. the various objects won are well within the powers of Agni and Soma to deliver to us. Note that Agni is once called urujr├бyas- (V.8.6, in this maс╣Зс╕Нala) and both Agni (III.5.8, V.24.3 [this maс╣Зс╕Н.], X.176.4, etc.) and Soma (I.91.15) can be subj.

of the verb uruс╣гy├б- тАШmake widenessтАЩ.

Griffith

Like as he is beheld such is he said to be.
They with effectual splendour in the floods have made
Earth yield us room enough and amply wide extent, great might invincible, with store of hero sons.

Genau wie es geschaut wurde, so wird es berichtet: Sie haben nach dem vollkommenen Abbild im Wasser die uns Raum gebende Erde, die weite Bahn, die gro├Яe mannhafte unentwegte Macht wiederhergestellt.

Grassmann

So wie jeder erblickt wird, so wird er auch eingeladen; mit ihrem heilvollen Widerscheine in den Wassern machten sie uns zugleich die grosse Erde ger├дumig und weit die Ausdehnung, und stark, heldenkr├дftig, unersch├╝tterlich die Macht.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe sage S┼лrya, advancing, accompanied by his bride, (the dawn), proceeds boldly, intent on combat with his enemies; may he on whom riches are dependent, secure our entire felicity, (and grant) a brilliant and everywhere protecting mansion.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(When) unwed, he pursues (women); once he has wives, he truly out(strips) (all) contenders with a mind that seeks conflictтАФ(as) the sun, the sage poet.
He with his goods near at hand will vanquish the (sunтАЩs) heat and will win shelter for us, which protects (our) patrimony on all sides.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Again my interpr. differs markedly from those of others. Again I think the unexpressed subj. of the whole vs. is Agni/Soma, not the sun (s┼л╠Бryaс╕е) with most others. The nom. s┼л╠Бryaс╕е is instead used to characterize both, since both Agni and Soma can be identified with the sun; that is, each is (equivalent to) the sun in his own way. Cf. тАЬthe sun of the lower realmтАЭ in 2a with reference to phenomena related to both Agni and Soma.

In p─Бda a I take the two adj. ├бgruс╕е тАШunmarriedтАЩ and j├бniv─Бn тАШpossessing wife/wivesтАЩ as expressing two stages in the development of Agni/Soma, rather than as paradoxically simultaneous with Geldner and Renou (Witzel Got┼Н interpr. resembles mine). The position of va├н supports an interpr. with two clauses. In the first stage Agni/Soma pursues females/wives; cf. VII.96.4 jan─лy├бnto nv ├бgravaс╕е тАЬbachelors in search of wives.тАЭ Again we have unidentified (and here unexpressed) plural females – in AgniтАЩs case I surmise they are the plants that supply firewood and/or the streams of ghee poured in the fire; in SomaтАЩs the cows, with whose milk he is mixed, or even the waters that swell him. Once Agni and Soma have тАЬmarriedтАЭ these females and are j├бniv─Бn тАШpossessed of wivesтАЩ, each can use the extra power acquired from these females to best his rivals. In this second clause I supply a second verb, perhaps a form of тИЪtс╣Э, because тИЪv─л does not otherwise occur with ├бti, whereas tutury─Бma+├бti is found in the next hymn (V.45.11).

In cd I take the verb vanavat in two senses, negative and positive, both well represented for this stem. With the obj. ghraс╣Гs├бm тАШheatтАЩ, the verb has the sense тАШwinтАЩ = тАШvanquishтАЩ, as in nearby V.29.9 ├бvanor ha ┼Ы├║с╣гс╣Зam тАЬyou combatted / vanquished ┼Ъuс╣гс╣ЗaтАЭ; with the obj. ┼Ы├бrma тАШshelterтАЩ, тАШwinтАЩ = тАШgainтАЩ. I take r├бkс╣гantam as a qualifier of ┼Ы├бrma (more or less; see below), with the participle itself taking the obj. g├бyam (тАЬshelter тАж protecting our patrimonyтАЭ). In taking g├бyam as obj. of r├бkс╣гantam I am flg. Oldenberg, who cites as parallel I.74.2 ├бrakс╣гad d─Б┼Ы├║с╣гe g├бyam, which seems pretty conclusive to me. There are also two passages (VI.71.3/X.66.3) in which g├бyam is the object of the semantically parallel verb p├бri тИЪp─Б тАШprotect all roundтАЩ (e.g., X.66.3 … p├бri p─Бhi no g├бyam); note p├бri immed. flg. r├бkс╣гantam here. By contrast, Geldner, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н all take g├бyam as an immed. object of vanavat, modified by r├бkс╣гantam, which itself governs ghraс╣Гs├бm (cf., e.g., Renou тАЬQuтАЩil nous assure une demeure prot├йgeant de toutes parts de (son) ardeur тАжтАЭ). This interpr. not only ignores the тИЪrakс╣г + g├бyam parallel, but also requires a significant attenuation of the meaning of тИЪvan (see RenouтАЩs n. on the p─Бda), and I also donтАЩt know of parallel uses of тИЪrakс╣г meaning тАШguard against / fromтАЩ. Against this we must balance one clear defect in my interpr., that ┼Ы├бrman- is neut. and the part. r├бkс╣гantam is masc. To account for the gender discrepancy I would suggest that the immediate referent of r├бkс╣гantam is not ┼Ы├бrma, but a different, underlying, masc. noun to which ┼Ы├бrma is an appositive – perhaps kс╣г├бyam тАШpeaceful dwellingтАЩ, as in I.133.7 van├│ti тАж kс╣г├бyam. Or it might be enough to invoke the distance between r├бkс╣гantam and ┼Ы├бrma in the hemistich, which might account for the gender mismatch. (I prefer the former, grammatically blameless, possibility. In this case the tr. might be slightly changed to тАЬwill win (peaceful dwelling) as shelter for us, protecting (our) patrimony on all sides.тАЭ)

Griffith

Surya the Sage, as if unwedded, with a Spouse, in battle-loving spirit moveth o’er the foes.
May he, self-excellent, grant us a sheltering home, a house that wards the fierce heat off on every side.

Geldner

Unverm├дhlt und doch beweibt ├╝berbiete er die Nebenbuhler streitlustigen Sinnes. Der Seher Surya m├╢ge ein Haus, das ringsum seine Glut abh├дlt, m├╢ge uns seinen Schutz zuwenden, er der alles Gute zu eigen hat.

Grassmann

Der weise Sonnengott geht unverm├дhlt oder verm├дhlt mit kampflustigem Muthe durch die Feinde; er schenke uns Sonnenschein, der rings unser Haus beschirmt, und Schutz er, der sch├╢n mit Gut zur Hand ist.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe (pious man) proceeds to you, most excellent (of the gods, who are indicated) by the sign of this moving (revolution); who are hymned by the с╣Ыс╣гis in whose praises youyr name (is glorified); he obtains that blessing by his devotion, on whatsoever (his desire) has been fixed; and he also, who of his own accord offers (worship) acquires abundant (reward).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

By the sign of this moving revolution: asya yatunasya ketuna is the text which is explained: karmaс╣Зoday─Бdi lakс╣гaс╣Зena, characterized by functions such as rising and the like; he also…acquires abundant reward: ya u svayam vahate so aram karat = he who, not urged by another, entertains of his own mind the hope of reward, he does, much, or enough; atyartham karoti is one explanation; another is, atyartham kury─Бt, let him do much, or enough

Jamison Brereton

He [=poet] pursues the older sonority of the seers by means of (you [=Agni/Soma]), the beacon of this arrangement [=sacrifice]. Among which (females [=waters/cows/insights]) your name (is),
in whatever (place) it has been set, he will find it [=sonority of the seers] through his industry. He who makes the journey by himself, he will
get it right.

Jamison Brereton Notes

OldenbergтАЩs stark statement about this vs., тАЬIch wage keine Erkl├дrung,тАЭ is somewhat lowering to the spirit. Nonetheless, I think some sense can be wrung from it. As I said in the published introduction, I think a new figure enters the scene at this, the midpoint of the hymn – namely the poet, learning and perfecting his craft – and in my opinion he is the subject of the vs., though Agni and Soma are still very much present.

By my interpr. the unnamed would-be poet тАЬpursues/proceeds towards/practicesтАЭ (carati) тАЬthe older (/superior) sonority of the seersтАЭ (jy─Б╠Бy─Бс╣Гsam тАж с╣Ыс╣гisvar├бm), that is, he imitates and aspires to the sound of the legendary poet-seers who preceded him. He does so by means of asy├б yat├║nasya ket├║n─Б тАЬby the beacon of this yat├║na.тАЭ Unfortunately yat├║na- is a hapax, and there is no agreement on its meaning or etym. (see, e.g., EWA s.v.). However, we can approach the sense of this phrase from several angles. The most promising of these, in my opinion, is the recognition that the phrase yaj├▒├бsya ket├║- тАЬbeacon of the sacrificeтАЭ is a very common expression in the RV (I.96.16, I.113.19, etc. etc., incl. in this maс╣Зс╕Нala V.11.1).

Moreover, both Agni and Soma are identified as yaj├▒├бsya ket├║-; Agni: the three passages just cited, plus I.1127.6, III.11.3, etc.; Soma: IX.86.7. I take yat├║na- as a nonce substitute for yaj├▒├б-, with vaguely similar phonology, built to тИЪyat тАШarrangeтАЩ.

(This is the root affiliation suggested by most [cf., e.g., AiG II.2.485].) Unfortunately this root does not seem to be generally used in ritual context, but a generalized abstract тАШarrangementтАЩ can stand in for the more specific тАШsacrificeтАЩ. This hapax yat├║na- echoes immed. following instr. ket├║n─Б (though obviously the morphology is different) and also reminds us of the two unexpected -u-stems in 5: t├бru- and -sv├бru-.

Putting all this together, I would claim that the poet is pursuing the model of the previous poets by means of the beacon of the sacrifice (/тАШarrangementтАЩ), and that this beacon is actually the usual amalgam of Agni and Soma, who, as we just saw, can be so called. In other words, the shimmering leaders of the sacrifice, the two ritual substances fire and soma, provide the (en)light(enment) as the poet follows the progress of the sacrifice as it leads him to his poetic goal.

Unlike most interpr. I take the loc. rel. cl. ending b (y─Б╠Бsu n─Б╠Бma te) as parallel to the one beginning c (y─Б╠Бdс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыmin dh─Б╠Бyi), also with a loc. expression. Both remind us of 2d тАж с╣Ыt├б ─Бsa n─Б╠Бma te; besides the identical final n─Б╠Бma te, note the echo between y─Б╠Бsu and ─Бsa. The fem. loc. y─Б╠Бsu refers to the now familiar mix of fem. plurals – waters, cows [=milk], streams of ghee – with the possible addition of fem. words for mental and verbal products: insights, hymns, etc. In any case the poet finds the jy─Б╠Бy─Бс╣Гsam тАж с╣Ыс╣гisvar├бm he is looking for at the place where the names of Agni and Soma have been set – that is, at the heart of the sacrifice. I take the referent of t├бm to be с╣Ыс╣гisv├бra- of b. To find it he needs not only the beacon provided by Agni/Soma but also his own industry (apasy─Б╠Б-).

The final p─Бda reiterates that the poet must rely on himself: he must make the journey to poetic mastery by himself, and if he does, he will get it (that is, the poetry) right. The phrasal verb ├бraс╣Г karat of course reminds us of alaс╣Гk─Бra, the later technical term for poetic ornament. Cf. already in the RV VII.29.3 k─Б╠Бte asty ├бraс╣Гkrti╠е с╕е s┼лkta├нс╕е for a connection between hymns and proper preparation. (Contrary to the standard tr., I do not think that y├б u svay├бс╣Г v├бhate has anything to do with marriage and bringing the bride home.)

Griffith

Thy name, sung forth by Rsis in these hymns of ours, goes to the loftier One with this swift mover’s light.
By skill he wins the boon whereon his heart is set: he who bestirs himself shall bring the thing to pass.

рдЗрдпрдордкрд┐ рд╕реМрд░реА ред рдЖрд╕рд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддреАрдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рдВ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рд╡рддреНрдкрд░реНрдпрд╡рд╕рд╛рдирднреВрддрдВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдореН рдЕрдЧреНрд░рд┐рдорд╛ рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдВ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдард╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреАрдпрд╛ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГ рдЕрд╡ рддрд╕реНрдереЗ рдЕрд╡рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рдЖрд╕рд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдирд╛рдореГрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд░рд┐рддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ ред рд╕рд╡рдирдореНред рд╕реВрдпрддреЗ рд╕реЛрдореЛрд╜рддреНрд░реЗрддрд┐ рд╕рд╡рдирдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдЧреГрд╣рдореН ред рди рд░рд┐рд╖реНрдпрддрд┐ рди рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕реНрдпрддреЗ ред рдХрд┐рдВрддреБ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрдзрддреЗ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдирд╛рдпрддрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдгрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рддрддреНрд╕рд╡рдирдорд┐рддрд┐ ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдЧреГрд╣реЗ рдХреНрд░рд╡рдгрд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдХрд░реНрддреБрдГ рд╣рд╛рд░реНрджрд┐ рд╣реГрджрдпрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рд╣реГрджрдпрдЧрддрдВ рдХрд╛рдореНрдпрдВ рдлрд▓рдВ рди рд░реЗрдЬрддреЗ рди рд╡рд┐рдЪрд▓рддрд┐ ред рди рдореГрд╖рд╛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рдпрддреНрд░ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрдЧреГрд╣реЗ рдорддрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГ рдкреВрддрдмрдиреНрдзрдиреА рдкреВрддрдВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдореН рдЕрдиреБрдмрдзреНрдирддреА рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрддреЗ рдЕрддреНрд░ рди рд░реЗрдЬрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe chief of these (our praises) proceed to the ocean-like sun; that chamber of sacrifice fails not in which (his praises) are prolonged; there are heart’s desire of the worshiper is not disappointed where the mind is known to be attached to the pure (sun).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The foremost of these (females) has stepped down into the ocean (of soma). The pressing is not harmed into which she is guided.
Here the heart of the working poet [?] does not tremble, where the
thought is found that is his bond to the purified (soma/fire).

Jamison Brereton Notes

In my interpr., the first half of this vs. depicts the offering of ritual oblations, while the second one connects the poet, whom we first met in the previous vs., with this ritual activity.

The fem. phrase ─Бs─Бm тАж agrim─Б╠БтАЬthe foremost (fem.) of these (fem.)тАЭ must refer yet again to the females weтАЩve met before: waters, cows, streams of ghee, as was just noted above. In p─Бda a the first such female goes down into the ocean (samudr├бm); this could be the ocean of soma as often or the undulating flames of the ritual fire (see I.71.7 where the offerings entering the fire are compared to streams entering a samudr├б-). In p─Бda b the word s├бvana- тАШpressingтАЩ limits the reference to soma, but throughout the hymn we have seen phraseology that is more appropriate to one of the gods than to the other (generally, in fact, in favor of Agni). That b is a clear soma p─Бda does not, in my opinion, invalidate the general interpr. of the hymn as applicable simultaneously to the two gods. It is also worth noting in passing that s├бvana-, which occurs approx. 100x in the RV, is found only once in the IXth Maс╣Зс╕Нala.

Why it is necessary to state that the pressing is not harmed when the female enters it is not clear. Perhaps it is meant as understatement: it is not only not harmed, but is positively benefitted. Or perhaps there is a whiff of the fear of contamination caused by females.

P─Бda c brings us another impenetrable hapax, kravaс╣З├б-. The first thing to notice, perhaps, is that it rhymes with s├бvana- (though it does not match it in accent).

As with the hapax yat├║na- in 8a beside ket├║n─Б, one of the contributors to the formation of the hapax may be phonological echo. There is, as usual, no consensus on the etym. or sense of the word; Geldner and Renou (inter alia) take it as a PN – a convenient strategy, but in a hymn that contains no other PNs (at least in my opinion) an unlikely solution. Witzel Got┼Н take it as тАШOpferschl├дchterтАЩ, related to krav├нs-, a suggestion mentioned but not endorsed by Oldenberg (see also EWA s.v.). My own tentative suggestion has no better support. I consider it, like kr├нvi- in 4d, to be another phonologically scrambled encoding of the word kav├н-, here perhaps crossed with a form of тИЪkс╣Ы, hence my tr. тАШworking poetтАЩ. (A putative participial -─Бс╣З├б- might have been remodeled under pressure from s├бvana- in b.) Although I will not attempt a spirited defense of this despairing attempt, it does have certain points in its favor.

First, if kriv├н- in 4d and kravaс╣З├б- here are both deformations of kav├н-, which itself appears in 7b, we have a little ring of references to the poet in the midsection of this hymn. More important, reference to a poet in 9c fits well with the subordinate clause in 9d. Just at the time when oblation is made and the soma is prepared (9ab), the poet who is not intimidated (тАЬhis heart does not trembleтАЭ) finds the poetic expression (mat├н-) that connects him to the purified ritual substances soma and fire. (Though p┼лt├б- almost always refers to soma and never to fire directly, other forms derived from the root тИЪp┼л, like p─Бvak├б-, are standard qualifiers of Agni.) If I am correct that vs. 8 depicts an apprentice or neophyte poet embarking on his journey to poetic mastery, then 9cd shows him achieving his first success at a climactic moment in the sacrifice, which provides inspiration to his undaunted heart.

Griffith

The chief and best of these abideth in the sea, nor doth libation fail wherein it is prolonged.
The heart of him who praiseth trembleth not in fear there where the hymn is found connected with the pure.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe verily (it to be glorified); let us, with the plural asant thoughts of Kс╣гatra, Manasa, Avada, Vajada, Sadhri and Avatsara, fill up the invigorating food (the portion) to be shared by the wise.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Kс╣гatra, manasa…: these are the names of the с╣Ыс╣гis

Jamison Brereton

For he (has a bond) with the insights of the mental lordship of the one deserving the sacrifice, who speaks just so and aims toward the
same goal.
With the delightful (poems) [/lusty (warriors)] of the stealthy one we shall win the most expansive prize, to be brought to success only by the wise.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner and Renou deal with the difficulties of this vs. by taking all (or almost all) the genitives as PN, a solution going back to S─Бyaс╣Зa.: (Geldner) Kс╣гatra, Manasa, Yajata, Sadhri, and Avats─Бra, to which Renou adds Ev─Бvada. (Note that the Anukr. ascribes this hymn to one Avats─Бra K─Б┼Ыyapa, but this is, in my opinion, based on a later misunderstanding of this vs.) Since all of these forms, on the one hand, either are, or bear a strong resemblance to, real words in the language and, on the other, are not used as names elsewhere, the Geldner/Renou PN strategy seems like an evasion of responsibility. It is to the credit of Witzel Got┼Н that this makeshift is not resorted to; all these forms are given full lexical weight. And the Witzel Got┼Н interpr. of ab is not too distant from mine, in that they take the subject to be a/the poet, who has some connection to the c├нtti- of the figures mentioned in the gen. (Witzel Got┼Н: тАЬDenn er is es [ein с╣Ъс╣гi?] durch die Einsichten dessen тАжтАЭ), though our treatments of the genitives differ.

My interpr. of the relation between s├б and c├нttibhiс╕е calls upon the тАШbondтАЩ (b├бndhan─л) of 9d, where the poet found the thought that binds him to the ritual substances soma and fire. I think 10ab elaborates on this notion, by ascribing the insights to Soma and Agni themselves.

The second set of genitives, ev─Бvad├бsya yajat├бsya s├бdhreс╕е in p─Бda b, by my interpr. refer to Agni and Soma simultaneously. Both Agni and Soma are elsewhere described as yajat├б- тАШworthy of the sacrificeтАЩ (Agni, e.g., I.128.8; Soma, e.g., IX.86.14). Assuming that the hapax ev─Бvad├б- has the sense тАШspeaking thusтАЩ it transparently presents, it can apply to both Agni and Soma because both substances are often said to speak or sound: for Agni cf., e.g., VI.4.4, 13.6; for Soma cf. esp.

IX.113.4, 6. As for s├бdhreс╕е, the obvious connection with sadhry├а├▒c- тАШdirected towards the same goalтАЩ is affirmed by Grassmann, AiG II.2.154, EWA s.v sadhr─л╠Бm, etc. It is the morphology that is puzzling, made more complex by the fact that it should be trisyllabic with a short penultimate, hence *s├бdhriyaс╕е? (so approx. Grassmann). (Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition simply pronounce the p─Бda as having 11 syllables, but since this would be a metrical irregularity in a Jagat─л hymn and since there is no independent stem *s├бdhri- to which s├бdhreс╕е would obviously belong, it seems better to perform the metrical distraction.) I have no answer for the morphology or for the accent, but given the morphological flexibility in the rest of this hymn, this is not surprising.) The тАЬsame goalтАЭ that Agni/Soma are aiming at is the eloquence that the poet is also seeking to harness.

I take this second set of genitives, referring to Agni/Soma, as dependent on, not parallel to, the first pair of genitives, kс╣гatr├бsya manas├бsya. My тАЬmental lordshipтАЭ refers to the mastery those two gods have of the poetry and the insights that produce it. The adj. manas├б- is a hapax, but it fits a common pattern of deriving suffixaccented thematic adjectives to s-stems; cf., e.g., vacas├б- тАШeloquentтАЩ to v├бcas- тАШspeechтАЩ and AiG II.2.136.

The second hemistich takes advantage of the double meaning of r├бс╣Зa- and its derivatives (r├бс╣Зa- тАШjoy / battleтАЩ, raс╣Зv├б- тАШdelightful / battle-lustyтАЩ, etc.). I take the referent of the pl. r├бс╣Зvabhiс╕е to be poems (or perhaps the тАШinsightsтАЩ c├нtti- of p─Бda a).

As warriors fighting alongside us they allow us to win the prize (spс╣Ыс╣Зav─Бma тАж v─Б╠Бjam), but as poems they are also delightful or joy-bringing. That winning the prize requires wisdom, not just brute strength, is expressed by vid├║с╣г─Б cid ├бrdhyam тАЬto be brought to success only by the wise,тАЭ a signal that it is insights or their products, poems, that are being deployed.

It remains to identify тАЬthe stealthy oneтАЭ (avats─Бr├б-), assuming as I do that it is not a PN. As I just noted, not only do Geldner and Renou (but not Witzel Got┼Н) take it as a PN, but the Anukramaс╣З─л ascribes this hymn to Avats─Бra K─Б┼Ыyapa, who is also purported to be the Soma hymns IX.53-60, a group of short G─Бyatr─л hymns with no obvious connection to V.44. It seems obvious to connect the word with the lexeme ├бva тИЪtsar and the root тИЪtsar тАШcreepтАЩ more generally. The root is poorly attested, and ├бva тИЪtsar only occurs once (I.71.5 in the notorious heavenly incest story). Agni is once the subject of тИЪtsar (I.145.4), and the occurrence of ├бva тИЪtsar is found in an Agni hymn (though not with Agni as subject). Soma is never subject of this verb, but its rarity makes this unsurprising. Both Agni and Soma can be conceived of as creeping or stealthy because of their slow and gradual movements – Agni as the fire slowly catches in the kindling, Soma as the juice spreads across the filter.

Griffith

For it is he: with though to of Ksatra, Manasa, of Yajata, and Sadhri, and Evavada,
With Avatsara’s sweet songs will we strive to win the mightiest strength which even he who knows should gain.

Geldner

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSwift is the excessive and girth-distending inebriation of Vi┼Ыvav─Бr─Б, Yajata and M─Бyin; (by drinking) of these (juices) they urge one another to drink; they find the copious draught the prompt giver of intoxication.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Swift iс╣г..inebriation: ┼Ыyena ─Бs─Бm aditiс╕е kakс╣гyo madaс╕е: ┼Ыyena = ┼Ы─лghra, quick;

Aditi = atisamс╣Ыddhaс╕е;

─Аs─Бm = of these, Soma juices;

Mada = intoxication, is the devat─Б of the verse

Jamison Brereton

(While still) a falcon, (soma) is unboundedness for these (females [=poems/waters/cows]); (when it becomes) the exhilarating drink, it is their girdingтАФfor the one deserving the sacrifice, provided with all desirable things, master of artifice.
They [=priests] make (the females) set their goal to go to one after the other (of Soma and Agni) in turn. They know (that) unharnessing
and drinking in rounds (are) at hand.

Jamison Brereton Notes

If it is possible for this hymn to get more obscure, it does so in this vs. (Note that Oldenberg simply gives up in vss. 11-13.) Nonetheless, I think a consistent interpr. can be constructed and one that fits well with the increasing pace of the depiction of the ritual in the last few vss. The theme that unifies the vs. is that of ritual binding and unbinding – conveyed by the words ├бditi-, which I take as the abstract тАШunboundednessтАЩ not the name of the goddess, kakс╣гy├а- тАШgirdingтАЩ, and viс╣г─Б╠Бna- тАШunharnessingтАЩ.

The first half of p─Бda a (┼Ыyen├б ─Бs─Бm ├бditiс╕е) refers to the pre-ritual situation.

While Soma is still a falcon, swooping about in freedom before the sacrifice begins, he is/represents freedom also for the classes of females we keep encountering: waters, cows, hymns. Neither the waters nor the cows (=milk) have taken on their ritual roles, and the words have not yet been pressed into service as ritual speech. (ItтАЩs important to note that Soma himself is often called a ┼Ыyen├б- in IX; the bird is not simply the conveyor of the stolen soma.) In the second half of p─Бda a (kakс╣гy├▓ m├бdaс╕е) Soma has been transformed into the m├бda-, the exhilarating ritual drink, and that change in turn brings about the girding of the female entities in question. They are hitched up in their various ritual roles, and the sacrifice begins. This ritual commencement is both for the benefit of and involves the active participation of the two gods, Soma and Agni. It is thus that I interpret the genitives in p─Бda b (vi┼Ыv├бv─Бrasya yajat├бsya m─Бy├нnaс╕е (note the recurrence of yajat├бsya from 10b), also referring, in my opinion, to Agni/Soma.

(Once again both Geldner and Renou take all three genitives as PNs; once again Witzel Got┼Н do not.) In p─Бda c I take the priests as the subject of arthayanti тАШcause to seek as goalтАЩ.

They are now directing the ritual proceedings. The first object of arthayanti is unexpressed, in my view: it is the female ritual elements, waters, milk, hymns. The priests send them to their ritual tasks, the waters and the cowsтАЩ milk to soma, the hymns to Soma and Agni. The two gods are here represented by the ─Бmreс╕Нita any├бm- anyam тАШthe one, the other; one after the otherтАЩ. So far in the hymn the two gods have been fused into one, verbally speaking; here the ─Бmreс╕Нita is an intermediate step towards separating them, a step that allows for the introduction of a third god, Indra, in the next vs. In p─Бda d the priests realize that with the mobilization of all the elements of the ritual performance – the soma, the ritual fire, the waters, milk, and hymns – the climax of the sacrifice has been reached. The unharnessing of these elements can take place because all that remains is for the prepared soma to be drunk. This sets the stage for the premier soma-drinker, Indra, to appear on the scene, which he does in the next vs. The parallel forms viс╣г─Б╠Бс╣Зam parip─Б╠Бnam are both best taken as -ana-nouns to -─Б╠Б-roots, although Grassmann identifies the first as a root participle. Cf. AiG II.2.193.

Griffith

The sacred hymns love him who wakes and watches: to him who watches come the Sama verses.
This Soma saith unto the man who watches, I rest and have my dwelling in thy friendship.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╢реНрдпреЗрдирдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреАрдпрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╢реНрд╡рдГ (рдЖрд╕рд╛рдореН) рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдирд╛рдореН (рдЕрджрд┐рддрд┐рдГ) рдЕрд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢рд┐рдиреА рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐рдГ (рдХрдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдГ) рдХрдХреНрд╖рд╛рд╕реБ рднрд╡рдГ (рдорджрдГ) рдЖрдирдиреНрджрдГ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╡рд╛рд░рд╕реНрдп) рд╕рдордЧреНрд░рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд░рдгреАрдпрд╕реНрдп (рдпрдЬрддрд╕реНрдп) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд╕реНрдп (рдорд╛рдпрд┐рдирдГ) рдХреБрддреНрд╕рд┐рддрд╛ рдорд╛рдпрд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдпрд╕реНрдп рддрд╕реНрдп (рд╕рдореН) (рдЕрдиреНрдпрдордиреНрдпрдореН) (рдЕрд░реНрдердпрдиреНрддрд┐) рдЕрд░реНрдердВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ (рдПрддрд╡реЗ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреБрдореН (рд╡рд┐рджреБрдГ) рдЬрд╛рдирдиреНрддрд┐ (рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╛рдгрдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдореН (рдкрд░рд┐рдкрд╛рдирдореН) рдкрд░рд┐рддрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреЛ рдкрд╛рдирдореН (рдЕрдиреНрддрд┐) рд╕рдореАрдкреЗ (рддреЗ) реерезрезрее

English translation:

тАЬMay Sad─Бpс╣Ыс╣Зa, Yajata, Bahuvс╣Ыkta, ┼Ъrutavit, Tarya, associated with you, destoy, your foes; the с╣Ыс╣гi obtains his desires in both (worlds), and shines brightly, whenever he adores with well-mingled (offerings and praises) the host (of heaven).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Sad─Бpс╣Ыс╣Зa… names of с╣Ыс╣гis

Jamison Brereton

The one worthy of the sacrifice, always granting, has smashed away hatreds. тАЬTwistedтАЭ (here) by the arms [=activity (of you, the priests)], finding (the praise) that is heard, he is surpassingly in partnership
with you.
He [=Indra] comes in response to both the choice ones [=Agni and
Soma], and he is radiant when he has a share in the troop [=Maruts] with their (chariots?) that drive forth easily.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As I just said, I think this vs. represents the epiphany of Indra, come to drink the just-prepared soma. Although, in keeping with the practice of the hymn, he is not named, the presence of a new actor in the hymn is strongly signaled by the verb phrase in p─Бda a: v├н dv├нс╣гo vadh─лt: Indra is almost always the subject of verb forms to the root тИЪvadh. Although the subject of p─Бda a is also called yajat├б-, a word used in the two preceding vss. (10b, 11b) of Agni/Soma (in my opinion), тАШworthy of the sacrificeтАЩ is a generic descriptor of gods, is used elsewhere of Indra (e.g., II.14.10), and can be so applied here. And тАШalways givingтАЩ (sad─Бpс╣Ыс╣Зa, though a hapax, is a good description of Indra – or at least as we wish him to be.

In b Geldner and Renou take the three words b─Бhuvс╣Ыkt├бс╕е ┼Ыrutav├нt t├бryaс╕е as PNs yet again. I think they are all further qualifications of Indra. The first depicts the physical actions of the priest, who by the ritual activities performed by their arms (b─Бh├║-), тАЬtwistтАЭ Indra to the ritual ground. (For the use of тИЪvс╣Ыj to refer to bringing a god to oneтАЩs ritual, see VIII.76.1.) There is also a sly echo of the common bahuvr─лhi vс╣Ыkt├бbarhis- тАШhaving twisted ritual grassтАЩ, a ritual action that would indeed by performed by the priestsтАЩ arms. Indra is also easily qualified as ┼Ыruta-v├нd- тАШfinding [/knowing] what is heard (=praise)тАЩ. The third term t├бryaс╕е, a hapax, is more difficult. It may simply be a -ya- deriv. to тИЪtс╣Э (see Witzel Got┼Н тАЬder ├Ьberwinder [?]тАЭ), though this isnтАЩt terribly satisfying morphologically. I tentatively take it as a primary comparative to тИЪtс╣Э, with the short suffixal form -yas- rather than -─лyas- (t├бr─лyas- 1x in nearby V.41.12); cf. n├бvyas- / n├бv─лyas-. In that case it would be an adverbially used neut.

(тАШsurpassinglyтАЩ) and the predicate is the vaс╕е s├бc─Б тАЬ(is in) partnership with you.тАЭ For another predicated p─Бda-final ENC + s├бc─Б see VIII.92.29 ├бdh─Б cid indra me s├бc─Б тАЬAnd so, Indra, (you are) in partnership with me.тАЭ The second hemistich begins with an explicitly marked dual ubh─Б╠БтАж v├бr─Б, separated by a nom. sg. s├б. Here we have the triad that has just, in this vs., interrupted the fused identification of Agni and Soma. With Indra represented by s├б, the two other gods are for the first time in the hymn separated into a grammatical pair (though see the forerunner any├бm-anyam in 11c), rather than sharing grammatically singular descriptors applicable to each. (For ubh─Б╠БтАж v├бr─Б referring to animate beings, see X.85.9, where the two are the A┼Ыvins – though in that case v├бrameans тАШwooerтАЩ.) Indra тАЬcomes in responseтАЭ (pr├бty eti) to these two, i.e., to the ritual fire where offerings will be made to him and to his own ritual drink. The second verb bh─Б╠Бti тАШis radiantтАЩ is not a typical Indraic verb, but p─Бda d with its reference to the gaс╣З├б- тАШtroop, throngтАЩ easily brings the rhetoric back to Indra and his close ties with the Maruts, so often identified as a gaс╣З├б-. The lexeme pr├б тИЪy─Б, found here in supray─Б╠Бvan- тАШdriving forth easilyтАЩ, is also particularly associated with the Maruts; cf. III.29.15 mar├║t─Бm iva pray─Б╠Бс╕е, and verbal instantiations like I.37.14 pr├б y─Бta, also I.165.13, V.53.12, 58.6. I’ve supplied ‘chariots’ because r├бtha- several times used in a simile with pra тИЪy─Б (IV.19.5, VII.74.6, IX.69.9).

Griffith

Sadaprna the holy, Tarya, Srutavit, and Bahuvrkta, joined with you, have slain the foes.
He gains his wish in both the worlds and brightly shines-when he adores the host with well-advancing steeds.
