Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSutambhara, is the ministrant priest of the instrumental tutor of the sacrifice, the causer of the upward ascent of all holy rites; the cow offers juicy (milk); the milk is distributed; announcing this in order (Avast─Бra) studies (the holy texts) without repose.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The ministrant priest: sutambharo yajam─Бnasya satpatiс╕е: satpatiс╕е = hot─Б;

Sutambhara = name of a с╣Ыс╣гi, etymologically, the bearer or offerer of the oblation; hence, possibly a metaphorical person nation and in the context, merely describes the effusion of the Soma

Jamison Brereton

Bearing the pressed (soma) of the sacrificer, master of the settlements, he [=poet] is the udder, the ladle of all visionary thoughts.
He bears the (two) milk-cows [=Heaven and Earth, or Agni and Soma]; the milk, full of sap, has been brought to perfection. The one who
recites following (his teacher), he learns, not the one who sleeps.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, in this last real vs. of the hymn I think the poet, who has been learning his trade, is extravagantly celebrated as the figure on whom the whole sacrifice depends and the representative of various sacrificial personnel and equipment. By contrast, Geldner and Renou once again opt for a PN, this time Sutambhara whom they consider to be the patron of the sacrifice. I take sutambhar├бas the transparent cmpd it appears to be, conforming to the model of other -bhar├бtatpuruс╣гas (cf., with acc. 1st member, puс╣гс╣нim-bhar├б-, v─Бjam-bhar├б-, etc.) For the underlying syntagm see VIII.66.7 sut├бm bhara, where the subject is a priest or similar figure (also IX.6.6 sut├бm bh├бr─Бya). I construe the gen. y├бjam─Бnasya with the 1st member sutam, though it could also be a gen. of benefit (тАШfor the sacrificerтАЩ) and loosely construed with the whole cmpd. I do not think it is dependent on s├бtpatiс╕е, pace Geldner, Renou, and Witzel Got┼Н.

The 2nd p─Бda identifies the poet with the source (the cowтАЩs udder, ┼л╠Бdhaс╕е) and distributor (the ladle or scoop, ud├б├▒canaс╕е) of all poetic visions (v├н┼Ыv─Бs─Бm тАж dhiy─Б╠Бm), which are here equated with ghee oblations. (For ud тИЪa├▒c meaning тАШturn / scoop upтАЩ, see V.83.8, AV X.29.8, etc.; in AB and ┼ЪB uda├▒cana- is a ‘dipping vessel’.) The conflation of poems with liquid offerings we have already met before in this hymn, though it is only here that the dh─л╠Б- is explicitly referred to.

In c the Pp and the standard interpr. take dhen┼л╠Бas the sandhi form of nom. sg.

dhen├║s before r-. This is of course perfectly possible; however, I take the form as given, as the dual nom./acc. of the same stem. By this interpr. the poet who was the subj. of ab remains the subj. here, with the -bhar├б- of the cmpd in p─Бda a extracted and converted into a finite injunctive bh├бrat. Who are the two milk-cows he bears? It is of course tempting to identify them as Agni and Soma, the pair that has been hiding in this hymn all along. And in part I think that is the correct answer: the poet, whose verbal formulations are the foundation of the sacrifice, thereby supports the two ritual substances (/gods) that provide the material realization of the sacrifice.

Agni and Soma would be called dhen┼л╠Бbecause of the benefits they provide through sacrifice. But dual dhen┼л╠Бis several times used of Heaven and Earth (of the other four occurrences, at last III.6.4, IV.23.10), so that the poet through his sacrificial labors may be supporting the whole cosmos. Moreover, the milk of Heaven and Earth has a special connection with poetry. Cf. the curious passage I.22.14 t├бyor ├нd ghrt├бvat p├бy ╠е o, v├нpr─Б rihanti dh─лt├нbhiс╕е тАЬThe inspired poets lick the ghee-filled milk of this very pair [=Heaven and Earth; see vs. 13] with their poetic insights,тАЭ though the meaning of this vs. is obscure (see comm. ad loc.). In any case their milk is brought to perfection (┼Ыi┼Ыriye) in the rest of the p─Бda.

Contra Narten (1987: 281) and K├╝mmel (p. 528), who follows her, in the published translation I take this med. pf. as passive, contrasting with the act. trans. a┼Ыi┼Ыrayuс╕е (2x). However, it is possible that the verb is transitive, as they take it, and the poet remains as subj.: тАЬhe brings/has brought their milk to perfection.тАЭ This might be preferable, in that it emphasizes the poetтАЩs control over the sacrifice and its cosmic resonances.

The final p─Бda of the vs., and thus of the hymn, brings us back, abruptly and somewhat reductively, to the poetтАЩs training: тАЬpay attention to your teacher; donтАЩt nod off or go wool-gathering.тАЭ The lexemes ├бnu тИЪbr┼л and ├бdhi тИЪi belong to pedagogical vocabulary (for the latter see Ap─Бl─Б VIII.91.3 and comm. ad loc.). The final phrase n├б svap├бn тАЬnot the one who sleepsтАЭ provides a transition to the final two responsive verses with their insistently repested j─Бg─Бra тАШis/stays awakeтАЩ.

Griffith

The worshipper’s defender is Sutambhara, producer and uplifter of all holy thoughts.
The milch-cow brought, sweet-flavoured milk was dealt around. Who speaks the bidding text knows this, not he who sleeps.

Grassmann

Der Besch├╝tzer des Opfernden, der den Soma herbeibringt, ist aller Gebete Euter und Sch├╢pfgef├дss ; er pflegte die Milchk├╝he, nahm an sich die Milch, nachsprechend ├╝berlegt er nicht schlummernd.

English translation:

тАЬHim who is ever vigilant, holy verses desire; to him who is ever vigilant sacred songs proceed; him who is ever vigilant the Soma thus addresses, I am always abiding in your fellowship.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who stays awake, him the verses desire; who stays awake, to him go the melodies.
Who stays awake, to him does this Soma say: тАЬI am at home in
fellowship with you.тАЭ с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

As was just noted, the final n├б svap├бn of 13d provides a segue into this two-verse appendix with its 6 occurrences of j─Бg─Бra тАШis/stays awakeтАЩ. The two vss.

are strictly responsive – so strictly responsive that the replacement of y├│ in abc by agn├нr produces an awkward set of 12-syllable lines with Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence, an awkwardness surely meant to call attention to their tight twinning. The vs. pair is structured as a riddle + solution, though, given what we have just waded through, not a very challenging puzzle. The focus seems to be on Agni, since he is the solution to the riddle; the balance of the two ritual substances found in the rest of the hymn (if I am correct) thus appears to be disturbed. But I do not think that this means that Agni is the sole subject of the hymn, as Scarlatta suggests in his final comment (in Witzel Got┼Н).

Rather the final word is found in the last p─Бda of both vss., the direct address of Soma to Agni (t├бm ay├бm s├│ma ─Бha тАЬto him does this Soma sayтАЭ): t├бv─Бh├бm asmi sakhy├й ny├▓kaс╕е тАЬI am at home in fellowship with you.тАЭ It is the fellowship of Agni and Soma, intimately joined here and identified by name, though neither of them was named previously in the hymn, that we are left with and that allows us to revisit the many obscurities that preceded this statement.

Griffith

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni is ever vigilant, and him holy verses desire; Agni is ever vigilant, and to him sacred songs proceed; Agni is ever vigilant, and him the Soma addresses, I am ever abiding in your fellowship.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni stays awake: him the verses desire. Agni stays awake: to him go the melodies.
Agni stays awake: to him does this Soma say, тАЬI am at home in
fellowship with you.тАЭ с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes
14-15 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As was just noted, the final n├б svap├бn of 13d provides a segue into this two-verse appendix with its 6 occurrences of j─Бg─Бra тАШis/stays awakeтАЩ. The two vss.

are strictly responsive – so strictly responsive that the replacement of y├│ in abc by agn├нr produces an awkward set of 12-syllable lines with Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence, an awkwardness surely meant to call attention to their tight twinning. The vs. pair is structured as a riddle + solution, though, given what we have just waded through, not a very challenging puzzle. The focus seems to be on Agni, since he is the solution to the riddle; the balance of the two ritual substances found in the rest of the hymn (if I am correct) thus appears to be disturbed. But I do not think that this means that Agni is the sole subject of the hymn, as Scarlatta suggests in his final comment (in Witzel Got┼Н).

Rather the final word is found in the last p─Бda of both vss., the direct address of Soma to Agni (t├бm ay├бm s├│ma ─Бha тАЬto him does this Soma sayтАЭ): t├бv─Бh├бm asmi sakhy├й ny├▓kaс╕е тАЬI am at home in fellowship with you.тАЭ It is the fellowship of Agni and Soma, intimately joined here and identified by name, though neither of them was named previously in the hymn, that we are left with and that allows us to revisit the many obscurities that preceded this statement.

Griffith

Agni is watchful, and the gcas love him; Agni is watchful, Sama verses seek him.
Agni is watchful, to him saith this Soma, I rest and have my dwelling in thy friendship.

Geldner

Agni ist wach geblieben, ihn lieben die Rikverse; Agni ist wach geblieben, zu ihm kommen die Sangesweisen. Agni ist wach geblieben, zu ihm spricht dieser Soma: “In deiner Freundschaft f├╝hle ich mich heimisch.

Grassmann

Agni ist wach, ihn lieben die Gebete, Agni ist wach, ihm str├╢men zu die Lieder, Agni ist wach, zu ihm spricht dieser Soma: ] An deiner Freundschaft habe ich Gefallen.

Elizarenkova

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬреА рдорд╛рдгрд╕реЗ рдЖрд│рд╢реА рдирд╕рддрд╛рдд. рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдереА, рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХ, рдЬрд┐рддреЗрдВрджреНрд░рд┐рдп рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдереА рдЕрд╕рддрд╛рдд рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдирд╛рдЪ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╡ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдг рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ. рее резрел рее
